<![endif]--><span style="font-size: 18pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b><span style="line-height: 115%;">Spiritual Message for the Day – Maha Mrityunjaya Mantra by Sri Swami Sivananda</span></b></span></p>
<p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times Digest© | 25 May 2014 17:29 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;"></span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><br style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;" /></span></span></strong></p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">&nbsp;</p>
<hr /><!--[if gte mso 9]><xml>
 <o:OfficeDocumentSettings>
  <o:AllowPNG/>
 </o:OfficeDocumentSettings>
</xml><![endif]--><!--[if gte mso 9]><xml>
 <o:OfficeDocumentSettings>
  <o:AllowPNG/>
 </o:OfficeDocumentSettings>
</xml><![endif]-->
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center">&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Maha Mrityunjaya Mantra</b></span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Divine Life Society Publication: </b><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/books/es307.htm#preface"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Yoga – Questions and Answers</b></a><a name="_GoBack"></a><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> by Sri Swami Sivananda</b></span></p>
<p style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">ॐ</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">त्र्यम्बकं</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">यजामहे</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><br /> </b><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">सुगन्धिं</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">पुष्टिवर्धनम्</b></span><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><br /> </b><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">उर्वारुकमिव</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">बन्धनान्</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><br /> </b><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">मृत्योर्मुक्षीय</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><span class="tooltip"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">मामृतात्</b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </b></span><span class="sanskrit"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">॥</b></span></span></p>
<p style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><i>Om Tryambakam yajamahe sugandhim pushti vardhanam,<br /> Urvaarukamiva bandhanaat mrityormuksheeya maamritat</i></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Meaning</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">We worship the three-eyed One (Lord Siva) who is fragrant and who nourishes well all beings; may He liberate us from death for the sake of Immortality even as the cucumber is severed from its bondage (to the creeper).</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">BENEFITS</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">1. This Maha Mrityunjaya Mantra is a life-giving Mantra. In these days, when life is very complex and accidents are an everyday affair, this Mantra wards off deaths by snake-bite, lightning, motor-accidents, fire-accidents, cycle-accidents, water-accidents, air-accidents and accidents of all descriptions. Besides, it has a great curative effect. Again, diseases pronounced incurable by doctors are cured by this Mantra, when chanted with sincerity, faith and devotion. It is a weapon against diseases. It is a Mantra to conquer death.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">2. It is also a Moksha Mantra. It bestows long life (Deergha Ayush), peace (Shanti), wealth (Aishwarya), prosperity (Pushti), satisfaction (Tushti) and Immortality (Moksha).</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">3. On your birthday, repeat one lakh times this Mantra or at least 50,000; perform Havan and feed Sadhus, the poor and the sick. This will bestow on you long life, peace and prosperity.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">4. When the mind becomes ripe with the true knowledge of Paramatma, the soul gets liberated from the bonds of birth and death. This is called <i>moksha. </i>The <i>Tryambaka mantra </i>epitomises the special kind of <i>moksha </i>which accrues by the grace of <i>Tryambaka, </i>the three-eyed Siva. The <i>mantra </i>conveys the meaning that one is released from mortality by the grace of Siva in the same way as the cucumber fruit gets separated from its stalk. Every fruit, when fully ripe, is sweet, though it may have been bitter or sour when unripe. Similarly, when the soul becomes ripe through devotion, it is filled with the sweetness and joy that come from <i>jnana. </i>All fruits fall down from the branches on top, at the roots below, signifying that the root is their source, sustenance and ultimate sanctuary. The ripe soul, however, is the fruit of the tree of <i>samsara, </i>whose roots are on top, <i>"Oordhva moolam," </i>and whose branches grow down below. So the passage of the liberated soul is upward, <i>Oordhvagati. </i>Strictly speaking, there is no <i>gati </i>or <i>going, </i>for the soul. It is released at the very place where it existed. That is why the example of cucumber fruit is given. This fruit does not fall down but gets detached from the stalk, or rather, the stalk gets itself detached even without the fruit knowing it. Similarly the liberated one does not give up the world; the world gives him up. Remembering that this life has been vouchsafed to us to get rid of future births and deaths, let us pray to the God of our heart, to obtain His grace to qualify for this kind of liberation of the soul, <i>"cucumber mukti."</i></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;" class="MsoHyperlink"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Excerpts from:</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Maha Mrityunjaya Mantra: </b><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/books/es307.htm#preface"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Yoga – Questions and Answers</b></a><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> by Sri Swami Sivananda</b></span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
